# Bybit bot (v28) ŌĆö worklog / reminders

## 2026-03-27 ŌĆö DeepSeek timeout follow-up + skip-noise cleanup + midterm v3

### DeepSeek timeout clarification
- `/ai` timeout looked like API/network latency, not token exhaustion.
- No persistent DeepSeek failures were found in `logs/errors.log` on the server.
- Updated `bot/deepseek_overlay.py`:
  - default timeout raised from `20s` to `30s`
  - added one retry on `requests.exceptions.Timeout`
  - short backoff between attempts

### Telegram skip-noise cleanup
- Found that repeated `notional too small` / `BELOW_MIN_QTY` alerts were sent directly with `tg_trade(...)`.
- Added shared throttled helper in `smart_pump_reversal_bot.py`:
  - `tg_skip_throttled(strategy_key, symbol, bucket, msg)`
- Applied it to:
  - `range`
  - `inplay`
  - `retest`
  - `midterm`
  - `sloped`
  - `flat`
  - `breakdown`
  - `ts132`
- Goal:
  - keep operator visibility
  - stop flooding Telegram with repeated skip alerts for the same symbol/reason

### Midterm follow-up
- `midterm_pullback_v2_focus` finished all `576/576` combinations.
- Best near-pass still sits just below the hard net threshold:
  - `net=7.78`
  - `PF=1.574`
  - `WR=54.1%`
  - `DD=1.82%`
  - `negative_months=2`
- Created:
  - `configs/autoresearch/midterm_pullback_v3_tiny_focus.json`
- Purpose:
  - tiny sweep around the only real near-pass region
  - try to push net above `+8%` without reopening DD or red-month count
- Started live local research run:
  - `midterm_pullback_v3_tiny_focus`

### Server rollout
- Deployed:
  - `smart_pump_reversal_bot.py`
  - `bot/deepseek_overlay.py`
- Restarted `bybot.service`
- Service returned `active`

### Small-account execution follow-up
- Investigated repeated `BREAKDOWN SKIP ... notional too small` alerts.
- Root cause was not a one-hour cooldown; it was small-account sizing:
  - `RISK_PER_TRADE_PCT=1.0`
  - `BREAKDOWN_RISK_MULT=0.10`
  - `MIN_NOTIONAL_USD=10`
- Added controlled min-qty fallback scaffolding for:
  - `sloped`
  - `flat`
  - `breakdown`
- Goal:
  - allow these sleeves to stretch gently up to the minimum executable size
  - only within capped multipliers
  - improve tradeability on a small account without blindly lifting global risk

### Midterm breakout from near-pass -> real pass
- `midterm_pullback_v3_tiny_focus` moved from near-pass to real passing region.
- Current best compact pass:
  - `net=8.19`
  - `PF=1.629`
  - `WR=55.7%`
  - `DD=1.48`
  - `negative_months=3`
  - `trades=61`
- Created explicit live bridge candidate file:
  - `configs/midterm_live_candidate_20260327.env`

### DeepSeek operator freedom (safe mode)
- Added first real operator layer in `smart_pump_reversal_bot.py`:
  - proactive no-trades alert
  - proactive websocket-health alert
  - proactive quiet-market scan/no-entry alert
  - auto trade review on closed trades
- Operator flow stays safe:
  - advisory only
  - writes shadow recommendations
  - can call DeepSeek for a short comment
  - does not mutate live config or deploy anything by itself

## 2026-03-26 ŌĆö live sleeve recovery + operator roadmap + entry-safety follow-up

### Live sleeve reality confirmed
- Checked fresh live journal after the last deploy.
- `sloped`, `flat`, and `breakdown` are no longer stuck on `skip_no_engine`.
- They now show real `sched` and `try` activity in live.
- Current blocker for these sleeves is no longer missing engines; it is downstream signal quality / gating.

### New issue found from live logs
- Live journal showed:
  - `RuntimeWarning: coroutine 'InPlayBreakoutWrapper.maybe_signal' was never awaited`
- Root cause:
  - `breakdown_live.py` used sync `signal()` in an async live path
  - that path ultimately touched async breakout wrapper logic

### Fixes prepared locally
- Added async path to `strategies/breakdown_live.py`:
  - `signal_async(...)`
- Updated `smart_pump_reversal_bot.py` to use async breakdown signal path in `try_breakdown_entry_async()`
- Added per-symbol entry lock scaffolding in `smart_pump_reversal_bot.py`
  - protects against two sleeves racing into the same symbol at the same time
- Added symbol-lock diagnostics counters for:
  - breakout
  - midterm
  - sloped
  - flat
  - breakdown
- Fixed TS132 init log path to avoid the same `log(...) is not defined` class of bug if TS132 is enabled later.

### Operator roadmap captured
- Added:
  - `docs/AI_OPERATOR_ROADMAP_20260326.md`
- Purpose:
  - define the path from advisory AI -> research operator -> approval-gated config steward -> portfolio supervisor
  - keep the AI useful and active without giving it unsafe live authority

### Server rollout
- Deployed small safety patch to live:
  - `smart_pump_reversal_bot.py`
  - `strategies/breakdown_live.py`
  - `bot/diagnostics.py`
- Restarted `bybot.service` at `2026-03-26 18:57 UTC`.
- Service is `active` on the new PID.
- `errors.log` stopped updating after the old breakdown async failures at `18:56:43 UTC`, which is a good early sign that the new async breakdown path is no longer tripping the previous runtime error.
- Next confirmation still needed:
  - fresh post-restart pulse from the new process
  - verify no new `breakdown signal error ... asyncio.run()` lines appear

```
ą¤čĆąĖ RR=2.0: ąĮčāąČąĄąĮ TP 0.14ŌĆō0.30% ŌåÆ fees > edge ŌåÆ ą╝ą░čéąĄą╝ą░čéąĖčćąĄčüą║ąĖ čāą▒čŗčéąŠčćąĮąŠ
```

**ąÆčŗą▓ąŠą┤:** EMA pullback ąĮą░ 5m čāą▒čŗčéąŠčćąĄąĮ ąĖąĘ-ąĘą░ fees. ąŁčéąŠ ąØąĢ ą┐čĆąŠą▒ą╗ąĄą╝ą░ ą░ą╗ą│ąŠčĆąĖčéą╝ą░ ŌĆö

### Quality Gate Fixed on Server
- Ran `sed -i` via SSH: `BREAKOUT_QUALITY_MIN_SCORE=0.48 ŌåÆ 0.0` on server `.env`
- Bot restarted (PID 532140). Bot is live and running.
- `ENABLE_BREAKOUT_TRADING=1` and `ENABLE_MIDTERM_TRADING=1` confirmed on server.

### ETH Midterm Pullback V2 (Research Only)
- Built `strategies/btc_eth_midterm_pullback_v2.py` ŌĆö sloped channel filter + dynamic TP + two-phase exits.
- Comparison vs V1 (360 days, forward simulation):
  - V1: 80 sigs, WR 55%, PF 2.30, TotalR +43.5R ŌåÉ BETTER
  - V2: 33 sigs, WR 51.5%, PF 2.01, TotalR +15.6R ŌåÉ WORSE
- **Conclusion**: Channel as entry filter is too restrictive. V1 stays in production.
- V2 file kept for future reference / V3 development.
- Key learning: channel TP works well (Avg R:R 2.89) but combined filter reduces quality.

### Flat Strategy (Sloped Channel) Analysis
- 794 flat backtest runs analysed from autoresearch.
- **Winner: LINKUSDT + ATOMUSDT, shorts only, alt_sloped_channel_v1**
  - 360 days, 20 trades, WR 70%, PF 3.85, Net PnL +11.6%, Max DD 1.8%
  - Config: ASC1_ALLOW_LONGS=0, ASC1_MAX_ABS_SLOPE_PCT=2.0, ASC1_MIN_RANGE_R2=0.25
- Adding more coins doesn't help much (SOL/AVAX/ETH stay at PF 3.74, same 20 trades)
- BNB adds 5 more trades but drops PF to 2.72
- **Action**: Deploy LINK+ATOM shorts after GitHub push.

### GitHub Push Status
- Local branch `codex/dynamic-symbol-filters` is 2 commits ahead of server.
- No GitHub SSH key on Mac, no `gh` CLI.
- Solution: `brew install gh && gh auth login` (browser-based, no tokens needed).
- Then: `git push origin codex/dynamic-symbol-filters`

## 2026-03-18 ŌĆö Full Audit + Strategy Integration + Quality Gate Fix

### Root Cause: Bot Not Trading
- **BREAKOUT_QUALITY_MIN_SCORE=0.52** blocked ALL live entries. Quality score computed from live spread/chase/slippage always < 0.52.
- **FIX**: Set BREAKOUT_QUALITY_MIN_SCORE=0.0. Quality boost still works (higher score = larger position).
- **Proof**: 360d backtest with quality=0: 717 trades, WR 65.1%, +$70.40, ALL 12 months positive.

### Sloped Channel (alt_sloped_channel_v1)
- Tested 11 coins individually. Only ATOM consistently profitable (WR 58.8%, PF 2.49, shorts only).
- Created `strategies/sloped_channel_live.py` ŌĆö live wrapper with per-symbol instances.
- Wired into `smart_pump_reversal_bot.py`:
  - Added `ENABLE_SLOPED_TRADING` flag, `SLOPED_TRY_EVERY_SEC`, `SLOPED_ENGINE`
  - Added `try_sloped_entry_async()` function
  - Added dispatch in main price handler
- Recommended config: ATOM only, shorts only, ASC1_ALLOW_LONGS=0, ASC1_ALLOW_SHORTS=1.

### Triple Screen v132 (friend's strategy)
- Already ported from PineScript in `archive/strategies_retired/triple_screen_v132.py`.
- Wired into `smart_pump_reversal_bot.py`:
  - Added `ENABLE_TS132_TRADING`, `TS132_TRY_EVERY_SEC`, `TS132_SYMBOLS`, `TS132_ENGINE`
  - Added `try_ts132_entry_async()` with `_TS132Store` adapter
  - Added dispatch in main price handler
- **360d Backtest Results**: Default settings LOSE money on ALL coins tested (16 coins). Best was KSM at 180d only.
- **Conclusion**: Needs per-coin autoresearch on server before live deployment.
  - Autoresearch config created: `configs/autoresearch/triple_screen_adaptive_v1.json`
  - DO NOT enable TS132_TRADING until autoresearch finds profitable configs.

### Combined Portfolio (Breakout + Sloped ATOM)
- 360d combined: 734 trades, ~64.8% WR, +$75.29, ALL 12 months positive, ~6.3%/month.
- Strategies are complementary (breakout=impulses, sloped=channel fades).

### Documents Created
- `docs/BOT_AUDIT_REPORT_20260318.docx` ŌĆö comprehensive audit report with tables
- `docs/AUDIT_20260318.md` ŌĆö audit markdown
- `docs/ENV_CHANGES_20260318.md` ŌĆö phased .env change plan
- `configs/autoresearch/flat_slope_adaptive_families_v1.json` ŌĆö sloped channel autoresearch
- `configs/autoresearch/triple_screen_adaptive_v1.json` ŌĆö triple screen autoresearch

### Deployment Plan
- Phase 1 (NOW): BREAKOUT_QUALITY_MIN_SCORE=0.0. Monitor breakout entries 1-2 weeks.
- Phase 2 (Next week): Enable SLOPED_TRADING with ATOM only.
- Phase 3 (2-3 weeks): Run autoresearch for TS132 + sloped families. Deploy winning configs only.
- Phase 4 (Month+): DeepSeek overlay, BTC strategies, expand sloped to new coins.

- 2026-03-09 19:42 UTC | equities pair-diversification filter | added optional `--forbid-pairs` support to `scripts/equities_monthly_research_sim.py` and tested whether bad months were coming from correlated high-beta pairings. - 2026-03-09 19:44 UTC | equities dynamic correlation filter probe | extended `scripts/equities_monthly_research_sim.py` with an optional dynamic pair filter based on rolling daily-return correlation (`--corr-lookback-days`, `--max-pair-corr`). On the current 5-name growth sleeve (`AMD,GOOGL,META,NVDA,TSLA`) with regime `55/55/2`, earnings blackout `5d/2d`, `top_n=2`, `hold=15`, `lookback=60`, a strict correlation cap of `0.55` delivered the best dynamic result: `20` months, `33` trades, `63.64%` trade winrate, `15/20` positive months (`75%`), compounded `+71.80%`, max monthly DD `-9.75%`. This underperformed the static `NVDA:TSLA` forbid-pair rule on total return, but improved max monthly DD materially and removed the need for a hardcoded one-off blacklist. Conclusion: a dynamic concentration/correlation filter is viable and may be the cleaner long-term path than static pair exclusions. | done
- 2026-03-09 19:56 UTC | equities dynamic filter follow-up | ran three immediate follow-ups around the new dynamic correlation sleeve. Wider earnings blackout (`7d/3d`) made no difference at all versus the `5d/2d` baseline, a shorter hold (`12d`) reduced compounded return to `+66.80%`, and a stricter momentum threshold (`3%`) also made no difference on the selected 5-name universe. Conclusion: the current dynamic profile is relatively stable to nearby knob changes; the next useful improvement is likely a new idea (e.g. concentration by sector/cluster), not more local parameter twiddling. | done

- 2026-03-13 12:05 UTC | live health guard automation scaffold | added a stateful live-health guard on top of `scripts/run_live_diagnostics.sh`: new files `scripts/live_health_guard.py`, `scripts/run_live_health_guard.sh`, and `scripts/setup_cron_live_health_guard.sh`. The guard reads the existing diagnostics output, tracks prior state in `runtime/live_health_guard/state.json`, and only raises an incident when `CRITICAL` repeats for the configured number of windows (`LIVE_GUARD_ALERT_REPEAT`, default `2`) or when `CRITICAL_NO_CONNECT` happens immediately. Recovery clears the incident and can optionally send a recovery message. It uses the same `TG_TOKEN` + `TG_CHAT_ID/TG_CHAT` contract already used elsewhere. Local test-mode verified the intended behavior: first `CRITICAL` stays quiet, second consecutive `CRITICAL` opens the incident, and a later `OK` closes it. The strategy fits a simple linear-regression channel over the recent `1h` structure, requires coherent channel quality (`width`, `slope`, `R┬▓`), and then trades touch/reclaim at the lower band or touch/reject at the upper band with target just inside the opposite band. Initial broad router probes proved the new branch is operational but expensive; more importantly, the first useful signal appeared on single-symbol probes. All-side `180d` runs showed the slope idea is not universal: `LINK` base `+2.10`, `24` trades, PF `1.289`, DD `2.30` (`portfolio_20260313_155647_asc1_link_base_180d`), while `LTC`, `ETC`, `BCH`, and `BNB` were negative (`portfolio_20260313_155649_asc1_ltc_base_180d`, `portfolio_20260313_155648_asc1_etc_base_180d`, `portfolio_20260313_155656_asc1_bch_base_180d`, `portfolio_20260313_155723_asc1_bnb_base_180d`). Trade forensics showed why: on `LINK`, the positive edge sat almost entirely in the short-side, while longs dragged the profile down. Splitting the branch confirmed this. `LINK` short-only improved to `+5.43`, `14` trades, PF `3.123`, DD `0.83` (`portfolio_20260313_155844_asc1_link_short_base_180d`). `ATOM` short-only also turned positive at `+4.98`, `23` trades, PF `1.715`, DD `1.64` (`portfolio_20260313_160011_asc1_atom_short_base_180d`). `BCH`, `ETC`, `BNB`, and `LTC` short-only stayed weak/negative. The first honest mini-stack candidate is therefore `LINK + ATOM` slope-short, not a broad multi-alt slope bot. On `180d` it produced `+6.79`, `26` trades, PF `1.996`, DD `1.87` (`portfolio_20260313_160050_asc1_link_atom_short_base_180d`), and remained positive under explicit cost stress (`fee_bps=9`, `slippage_bps=12`): `+4.78`, PF `1.629`, DD `2.07` (`portfolio_20260313_160137_asc1_link_atom_short_coststress_180d`). Conclusion: the userŌĆÖs intuition about sloped levels was directionally correct, but the first clean edge is a narrow `LINK + ATOM` slope-short sidecar, not a universal flat bot. Next flat work should extend this branch carefully (for example via dynamic short-side selection or a matching sloped long companion), not revert to old `fb3` or broad `arr1` style long-reclaims. | done

- 2026-03-13 17:05 UTC | slope-short loss forensics + naive BE test | analyzed the new `LINK + ATOM + BNB` `slope_short_fade` family at trade-path level. Conclusion: the family really does need smarter profit-protection, but blunt always-on break-even is not the answer. - 2026-03-13 17:25 UTC | slope-short steepness cap breakthrough | tested a simpler, family-aware hypothesis directly on the current `LINK + ATOM + BNB` `slope_short_fade` basket: many losers were happening in overly steep channels, so instead of adding more exit machinery, we first tried capping the maximum absolute slope. Baseline `360d` benchmark remains `+7.35`, `54` trades, PF `1.408`, DD `4.03`, `8` positive / `4` negative months (`portfolio_20260313_171915_asc1_probe_baseline`). Conclusion: slope-family losses are not mainly ŌĆ£bad fakeoutsŌĆØ; a meaningful chunk comes from fading channels that are simply too steep for this mean-reversion logic. Next flat work should keep the family idea intact, but add steepness-aware gating and then re-test under explicit cost stress rather than defaulting to broad break-even logic. | done

### DeepSeek deploy safety fix

- Fixed `bot/deepseek_action_executor.py` so it now patches the active local env file instead of hardcoding `configs/server_clean.env`.
- New default resolution order:
  1. `DEEPSEEK_EXECUTOR_ENV_PATH`
  2. repo `.env` (preferred, gitignored)
  3. legacy fallback `configs/server_clean.env`
- Remote deploy target is now configurable via `DEEPSEEK_EXECUTOR_REMOTE_ENV_PATH` and defaults to `/root/by-bot/.env`, matching `bybot.service`.
- Fixed `scripts/deploy_session10.sh` to prefer local gitignored `.env` for `DEEPSEEK_API_KEY`, with `configs/server_clean.env` kept only as an explicit legacy fallback warning path.
- Syntax check passed for `bot/deepseek_action_executor.py`.

### Immediate recommendations

1. Stop treating tracked `configs/server_clean.env` as the source of truth for real secrets.
2. Redact it into an example-only file and rotate exposed credentials.
3. Keep using the 5-sleeve live stack, but add honest live observability for `flat` and `breakdown`.
4. Next research priority for core crypto remains `breakout side-split`, not breakout basket expansion.

### Live sleeve gate diagnostics ŌĆö 2026-03-26

- Continued investigating why `sloped/flat/breakdown` show `0 try` in live while their flags are enabled.
- Verified locally that scheduling blocks for all three sleeves are present in `detect()` and that the engines are initialized behind the matching env flags.
- Attempted a direct SSH/live log check, but the server timed out on port `22`, so no trustworthy remote root-cause was available from that path in this step.
- Added low-risk runtime diagnostics to [smart_pump_reversal_bot.py](/Users/nikolay.bulgakov/Documents/Work/bot-new/bybit-bot-clean-v28/smart_pump_reversal_bot.py) and [bot/diagnostics.py](/Users/nikolay.bulgakov/Documents/Work/bot-new/bybit-bot-clean-v28/bot/diagnostics.py):
  - new schedule counters: `sloped_sched`, `flat_sched`, `breakdown_sched`
  - new pre-signal gate counters for each sleeve:
    - `*_skip_no_engine`
    - `*_skip_trade_off`
    - `*_skip_no_client`
    - `*_skip_open_trade`
    - `*_skip_max_open`
    - `*_skip_portfolio`
    - `*_skip_cooldown`
- This patch does **not** change any trading logic or risk settings; it only makes the next live window diagnosable instead of ambiguous.
- Verified syntax cleanly with:
  - `python3 -m py_compile smart_pump_reversal_bot.py bot/diagnostics.py`
- Committed and pushed the diagnostics patch as `23701cd` (`Add live sleeve gate diagnostics`).
- Deployed the patch to the live server on `64.226.73.119` by copying:
  - `smart_pump_reversal_bot.py`
  - `bot/diagnostics.py`
- Restarted `bybot.service`; service returned `active` after restart.
- Immediate post-restart journal check confirmed the bot came back up cleanly, but a fresh new pulse with the added counters had not yet printed in the observed window.
- The next live window revealed the actual blocker:
  - `sloped_sched`, `flat_sched`, `breakdown_sched` were rising
  - `sloped_try/flat_try/breakdown_try` stayed at `0`
  - the dominant gate was `*_skip_no_engine`
- Added lazy engine re-initialization in [smart_pump_reversal_bot.py](/Users/nikolay.bulgakov/Documents/Work/bot-new/bybit-bot-clean-v28/smart_pump_reversal_bot.py) for:
  - `sloped`
  - `flat`
  - `breakdown`
- New behavior: if engine startup init failed or was lost, the sleeve will retry engine init on demand at first live attempt instead of staying permanently `None`.
- Lazy-init failures are throttled in logs (5 minutes) to avoid log spam while still surfacing the real exception.
- Verified syntax with:
  - `python3 -m py_compile smart_pump_reversal_bot.py`
- Root cause was then confirmed directly from server `errors.log`:
  - `[SLOPED] engine init fail: name 'log' is not defined`
  - same for `FLAT` and `BREAKDOWN`
- Fixed these init paths by replacing the non-existent `log()` success calls with safe `print()` logging in both:
  - startup engine init
  - lazy engine re-init
